B007UQ5Z1G|4.0|When Linkin Park began their experimentation period with 'Minutes to Midnight' it became difficult to tell whether I was still a fan or not. The first two albums were about balance between all members of the band, so when we started getting pieces that focused more on individual members we got some hit and miss music. 'Hands Held High' is still a joke to me and so are a few other songs they've written, but with 'Living Things' we have an album full of return to balance. Its still taking lessons from 'A Thousand Suns' with all of the electronica elements but overall its a successful album. Nothing special and nothing awful as a whole. When they announced that this would be a return to form I was excited. Then the single came out and I wasn't devastated, just disappointed. But it grew on me and the album itself has as well.<br /><br />1. Lost in the Echo 4/5 - Admittedly the first couple of notes threw me off a bit, but the overall sound and flow of this was a good way to start off the disc. A very 'LP-esque' track to help the transition from the last album to this balance.<br /><br />2. In My Remains 5/5 - Easily one of the more rock-focused tracks on the album, also focusing on Chester's vocals more than Shinoda's rap (Shinoda unleashed to his full element has proven to be a mistake for the band). Feels like it could have worked just as well on 'Minutes to Midnight' if all of Hahn's parts were taken out, but I'm glad it sounds the way it does. It has been a long time since the guitarists and Hahn met each other in the middle and this is where they do it for the first time in years. Excellent track.<br /><br />3. Burn it Down 3/5 - Here's the single, so no description of it is needed as its all over the radio. Overall not what I would call a stand-out track. Shinoda's bit hearkens back to their overtly-political leanings and doesn't really work for me, but Chester does decent with the vocals and I enjoy him here. To me this song felt more forced. Its grown on me butstill not a favorite from the album.<br /><br />4. Lies Greed Misery 1/5 - I hate this song with a burning passion. I never mind when the hip-hop influences leak through but this sounds like club music to me. From the Skrillex inspired sound to Chester's throw-your-hands-in-the-air chorus this just didn't do it for me. I have friends who love it and consider it a stand-out track, but this just felt more like something that would have been a semi-interesting b-side and nothing more.<br /><br />5. I'll Be Gone 5/5 - Another balanced track where you can feel all members working in unison. I absolutely love Hahn's light, floating overlay with Chester's soft vocals leading into a well performed chorus with a harmonizing Shinoda showing that not only is he a decent emcee but he can sing incredibly well (anyone remember the 'No Roads Left' b-side? Amazing track). This is without a doubt one of my favorite tracks in a few years.<br /><br />6. Castle of Glass 5/5 - Another example of what happens when the band steps outside of their wheelhouse and still maintains a balanced sound. Shinoda's string/horn arrangement sounds great here, and the soft vocals from both lead singers is outstanding. Semi-pretentious lyrics actually work well here. The sound is dangerous in the beginning but runs into a more soaring sounds that feels uplifting. Nice to see them pull things like this.<br /><br />7. Victimized 2/5 - A metal song could work for them in theory, but this quickly pumped out electric punk-metal song sounds cobbled together. This is the 'Blackout' of this album. Unimpressive, raging for no reason, and thundering its one I skip almost every time now.<br /><br />8. Roads Untraveled 5/5 - The music box intro with Shinoda's piano overlay is fantastic, I was hooked from the beginning. His vocals once again remind us how good of a singer he can really be, and his harmonizing chorus with Chester is amazing. Possibly the best song on the album right here. The split chord guitar segment with the beautiful vocals actually really perfects the song and I think this will be a staple live song.<br /><br />9. Skin to Bone 3/5 - This one felt like 'Burn it Down' to me. It was nothing fantastic, nothing awful. Its just there. It has an ok sound and some decent vocals, but it does nothing daring or exciting at all really. Sort of a background track. Crunchy beat at the end though, I enjoyed that.<br /><br />10. Until it Breaks 2/5 - I just can't stand when this song kicks in. The first half is absolutely brutal to me. Shinoda's distorted rap and his electronically repeated \\"Like dat dat...da da da dat dat\\" just annoys me. However, the last third of the song is quite beautiful. Brad Delson sings by himself for the first time on an LP album and the results are interesting and memorable. Its just rough to have to wade through the first bit of it. Reminds me of when I first heard 'Hands Held High' because it had an absolutely stunning outro but the song itself was ridiculously stupid.<br /><br />11. Tinfoil 2/5 - This was billed as an instrumental and was likened to 'A Cure for the Itch' and 'Session' but it is, in reality, just a drawn out intro to the next song. It seemed in this album that they learned to not have so many tracks full of dead air ('Empty Spaces', 'Fallout', etc...) but then there's this song. Its an interesting intro for the final track but had no business being separated from it.<br /><br />12. Powerless 4/5 - Excellent song with a crawl. Consider 'Tinfoil' just part of the song and you have an excellent track that clocks in at nearly 5 minutes to make it a long, balanced, great Linkin Park track.<br /><br />There we go guys, track by track breakdown. This is some of the better material they've released in the last 10 years, and I'm happy I bought it. On this album you won't find some of the stuff you did on the previous ones. There are no excessively-political tracks that leave the album lacking in a timeless quality, nothing like 'WhenThey Come For Me' that just complains that fans miss the style of the first two albums. This is just LP taking what they learned in their experimental phases and applying it with success. Not every track is a winner, but no doubt hardcore fans will worship this like they have every single song and album they've put out since their inception. For the rest of us its still a good album. Support the band, but from their website, Artist Direct, or from a show or something. Lets make this a higher selling album than the previous two and hopefully we'll get more of this quality of music.

B007XH6BPG|4.0|Personally I love this CD! All but the name. Squackett? Why not Hasquire? (Hay-Squire)I think they should have just labelled it as Squire and Hackett and left it at that. \\"Squackett\\" while humorous, may be a bit too corny. But anyway...As Steve and Chris are no longer \\"spring chickens\\" I was originally worried that this Cd would contain a lot of slow pensive numbers, exhibiting more of Steve's classical tastes with Chris filling on bass. I am happy to say that Squackett is not like that at all. The introductory title song \\"Life Within  A day\\" lets you know what you are in for with an upbeat number and a killer electric guitar solo by Steve.  A lot of the songs are very upbeat and even some of the slower songs that begin with only a classical guitar, end up unfolding into some amazingly rich and layered progressive music. On the second song \\"Tall Ships\\" Chris Squire creates one of the best, funkiest, bass lines I have ever heard from him. LWAD never really lets up.  Songs are all of a shorter nature with only two of the nine coming in at just over six minutes. The cd moves from song to song with no song ever wearing out its welcome by going on too long.<br /><br />Vocals are shared with some lead by Steve and Some lead by Chris with them ending up singing together on every song. Chris Squire's bass is \\"prevalent\\" in the mix, but never over powering. You can tell it is there and you know it is Chris but it is never pushed to the front of the mix so that is all you can hear.  His bass almost becomes another lead instrument. Steve Hackett's guitar work is his typical signature work featuring acoustic, classical and electric. One negative may be that the lyrics on some songs are very simplistic and repetitive, probably the most noticeable on \\"Storm Chaser\\".<br /><br />I have seen a couple of reviews of this CD that did not speak all that highly of it. One of the most ridiculous statements I heard was that it sounded like a Steve Hackett release. What's it supposed to sound like!? Yes? Genesis? Is everything going to magically change completely because Chris Squire is on bass? Chris has performed on Steve's songs before. This is just their first total collaboration. Yes, it does sound like a Steve Hackett release with Chris Squire on bass. And, to me, that is the beauty of it. I got exactly what I expected from a Hackett release with the wonderful added bonus of hearing Squires signature bass and his vocals. They seemed to use a lot of sensibility in creating this album. They never get too experimental and really do nothing to alienate either Hackett or Squire fans. Maybe one \\"epic\\" number would have been fun but I feel neither musician is at that point right now. The shorter songs allow them to showcase more varied styles and also appeal to the mass markets \\"pop\\" sensibility for more standard length songs.<br /><br />So...after all of this, should you purchase it? Most definitely! I feel a fan of either Squire or Hackett should enjoy LWAD. You get the best of both worlds. No 5 stars because I would have to be totally blown away by it or it would need to be compared in relationship to their other releases, of which there are none. It's a fine work, still better than 90% of the other meaningless dribble that now passes for pop/ rock music. It is as solid as any other Steve Hackett release and Chris Squire adds icing on the cake!

B0053VKP8S|5.0|I will say that the sole reason I bought this is that it was cheap. I didn't have much of an expectation that it would work like I wanted it to, but it was inexpensive enough that I figured it would be worth the gamble. My TV has a coaxial S/PDIF output, and my stereo amplifier only had analog RCA inputs, so the only way to route the audio through the stereo has been to juggle cords around or just forget about it. However, I just moved into a new house and figured that it would be a golden opportunity to set everything up like I wanted it, so I got this little device.<br /><br />First of all, it's small. Like, the size of a camera battery pack small. And, it's powered by USB. It comes with a wall wart so you can plug it in, but the energy it requires to run is practically negligible. It's switchable for TOSLINK or coaxial digital input, so no matter what you're plugging in to it, it'll work. Besides a loud pop when it synchronizes with the digital audio stream it's also seamless. One small caveat is this, however: make sure that your digital output from whatever device you're plugging in to it is set to output a 2 channel stereo stream. If you try to run Dolby 5.1 in to it your reward is a deafeningly loud machine-gun pulse of information it can't decode, and if you try to run mono in to it rather than splitting the signal between both channels, it only outputs on the left channel. For me this meant telling both the Xbox 360 AND the TV to output on 2 channel stereo; after that, it worked perfectly.<br /><br />I haven't gotten to use it a whole lot yet, but it seems to work perfectly with the DVD player, and I haven't noticed any jitter out of it. I also haven't tested it with a scratched DVD, so I have no idea what it will do when the stream is abruptly interrupted. So far, however, it seems to do everything the much more expensive units do, it can easily be hidden behind the stereo equipment, and works well with my aging (and ailing) stereo setup. One day I will probably buy an amplifier with a digital input; until then, I think this will work just fine.obably buy an amplifier with a digital input; until then, I think this will work just fine.

B007UQ5Z1G|5.0|I'll get this point out right now, if you are part of the music crowd who can't evolve past your initial introduction to a band you won't like this album. You haven't liked them for over five years, and you probably never will again. So all you Hybrid Theory and Meteora lovers, who are trapped in your small music box, just don't buy the album. No need to cry about it, they haven't been the band you loved for a long time, and they won't be going back so just move on. As for the rest of you still around, Living Things is pretty special. To me, it takes a lot of that experimental sound from A Thousand Suns but uses a song writing approach that mixes Midnights to Midnight with their first two albums. It's very clear that they could've never created this excellent new piece of work if it wasn't for the last album. This album has a lot of callings back to the old Linkin Park in terms of approach, not as much sound. What I mean is, rapping is back in a stronger way, the focus of personal songs have returned, and even the one instrumental before the final track is back. The sound as I brought up before takes a lot of the experimenting of A Thousand Suns but builds more focused songs like their previous efforts. Unlike A Thousand Suns, I believe this album is much easier to get into. With a great mix of heavy tracks, to slower more ballad like pieces Living Things is the culmination of Linkin Park's entire career. B005GG0MIS|5.0|Over the summer, I try to read books that have little to do with ministry, church or being a pastor. Enter The President's Club: Inside the World's Most Exclusive Fraternity by Nancy Gibbs & Michael Duffy. I can honestly say, there is no other book like this book. If you like history like I do, this book will simply fascinate you.<br /><br />The book starts with Truman and goes all the way until Obama, looking at how former President's interacted with sitting President's, what happened behind the scenes in their relationships, what was going on in the world during those presidencies.<br /><br />\\"I think we ought to organize a former presidents club,\\" said Herbert Hoover. \\"Fine,\\" answered Harry Truman, \\"You be the President of the club, and I will be the Secretary.\\" That unlikely exchange took place on January 20, 1953, at the inauguration of Dwight Eisenhower as President of the United States. Nevertheless, as Nancy Gibbs and Michael Duffy explain, the \\"club\\" really began in 1797 when George Washington retired from office and became, by his own design, the nation's first former president.<br /><br />In The Presidents Club, Gibbs and Duffy offer readers a treasury of insight into \\"the word's most exclusive fraternity.\\" From the time of George Washington's retirement, the nation has known relatively few periods without at least one living former President. The last time that happened followed the death of Lyndon Johnson in 1973. In contrast, when Bill Clinton took office in 1993, no less than five former Presidents were living. Four are living today.<br /><br />While I didn't read this book hoping to find leadership nuggets, they were everywhere in the book. One of the things the authors continually emphasized was the only person who can understand what being the President is like are those who have sat in that chair. I think that could be said for being a leader, running a company, leading a church. While being the President is a larger scope, and considerably more stressful than leading a church or running a business, there are some similarities. While I was a student pastor, I was convinced I knew what it was like to lead a church. Now that I lead a church, I realize how little I knew and how few people understand what it is like.<br /><br />From that perspective, it turned out to be a great leadership read.<br /><br />Here are a few things that jumped out to me:<br /><br />-Judgment is not the same as understanding.<br />-Their greatest problem was never doing what was right; their greatest problem was knowing what was right.<br />-Others may hate you, but those who hate you don't win unless you hate them, and then you destroy yourself.<br />-Don't confuse being `soft' with seeing the other guy's point of view.<br />-The greatest sin was remaining passive in the face of challenges.<br />-A good leader sets priorities--he doesn't just list.<br />-Promising great change and delivering it are two entirely different things.<br />-Once a president takes office, he learns that the office is its own arena, and that the tactics, tools, and talents that had helped him rise so far so fast were useful only to a point.<br />-Forced to choose between the unacceptable and the intolerable, leaders nonetheless have no choice but to lead.<br />-If you're doing big things, most of the time you're never going to be around to see them.<br />-If you aim for big change, you shouldn't expect to be rewarded by short-term history.

B007EW9ISM|5.0|If you are looking for a stylus to take notes or do homework with, this is it. Its exceptional build quality, sturdy design, and predictability make it the best writing and graphing stylus you can buy.<br /><br />The Cosmonaut isn't based on some fancy, next gen capacitative technology; and that's a good thing. Its lack of features is actually its best feature. There's nothing to replace, no electronic pressure sensing to glitch out or distract you, just pure, stylus functionality. It's all about the writing, swiping, and tapping and really, that's all that matters. Furthermore, its simplicity also makes it durable. Take tough aluminum and wrap it in even tougher rubber. This thing is built to last. Other rubber and mesh tipped styluses I bought started cracking or otherwise failing after about a month of hard use, this stylus just refuses to quit.<br /><br />I used the Cosmonaut for an entire quarter of college, which involved nightly math homework assignments, daily note taking, annotating more PDFs than I care to recall, and a whole lot of just screwing about on a tablet. I used it to write sentences and equations,to draw graphs and diagrams, and also to just navigate around the tablet interface. It excelled at all tasks. There is little to no friction with the screen surface (unlike cheaper rubber styluses) and even better, its stiffer tip makes it a lot more predictable and easy to control. Other rubber tipped styluses, even expensive ones like the Wacom Bamboo, simply compress too much when they're being used. This makes it somewhat difficult to figure out exactly where the line will show up. This is not a problem with the Cosmonaut.<br /><br />There are those who will say that if you want accuracy, you should go with the Adonit Jot, and if you are a professional artist who must know *exactly* where your line is being drawn down to the last pixel, well yeah, nothing beats being able to see the line as it's being drawn. But for the rest of us, the additional hassle of having to deal with replacement disks and a noisy writing experience is simply not worth it. Besides, the Cosmonaut is pretty good at drawing too. I'm not a serious artist by any means but I do dabble in sketches from time to time and I've had no problems with the Cosmonaut's lack of transparent tip. It's simply predictable to the point where that ceases to matter.<br /><br />That being said, it's not perfect. While I like the wide-bodied design, I personally think it's ergonomics would benefit from a slightly smaller diameter. This would also help with its other problem: weight. As far as I can tell, it's machined out of a solid chunk of aluminum, which is great for durability--it also gives it a satisfying heft. But you really feel that extra ounce or two after an hour straight of note-taking. Future iterations would benefit from a drilled-out aluminum core. In fact, I'm thinking about doing this myself with my friend's drill press.<br /><br />All in all, the Cosmonaut is as good a stylus as you're going to find on today's market. Its bare-bones design might turn some people off because there are more feature-rich styluses available at cheaper prices, but really, this is the one to get. Its predictability alone puts it head and shoulders above the competition and its durability only elevates it further.<br /><br />4.5/5 stars (this system doesn't support half stars unfortunately)<br /><br />Pros:<br />+Predictable writing and drawing<br />+Super durable design<br />+Little to no screen friction<br />+Simple, effective design that gets out of the way<br /><br />Cons:<br />-It's a bit fatter and heavier than I'd like in a writing implement

B007Y6OZE0|5.0|The Offspring's been a band known for a long time to bring surprises and unexpected left turns to every CD they release. Even Splinter, one of their shortest and most bare-bones albums, featured the 1930s style track \\"When You're In Prison\\" and the ska jam \\"Worst Hangover Ever.\\" Ixnay on the Hombre had more than its fair share of joke tracks and genre-exploring too, so I'm not sure why certain fans seem so up in arms by Days Go By branching out at times. Especially when *no* songs on here are as throwaway as the likes of When You're in Prison or Don't Pick It Up, and when Days Go By otherwise has some very consistently fast stuff reminiscent of CDs like Smash.<br /><br />This one takes off like a rocket with The Future is Now and Secrets From the Underground, songs that have a real sense of energy and lyrics that embody the punk rock spirit of rebellion and change. Things slow down a little for the title track, Days Go By, a fun and nostalgic single that I think fades so well into the next song, Turning Into You, which once again cranks things up. Reminds me a bit of the band Rise Against while at the same time feeling like Trust in You off the last album, this is another cool one with an awesome bridge. The CDs first act ends with Hurting As One, which sounds like a Smash song, no questions asked.<br /><br />And then we reach the mid-point, a place where there will probably be a lot of controversy among some. Cruisn' California (Bumpin in my Trunk) is clearly intended as a joke song, the Offspring likely enjoying the opportunity to spoof the zillions of California-themed party songs and it's actually pretty catchy. That said, I do think they should have left it off the album, as I just don't think it fits all that well and its inclusion is probably not worth the anger of certain fans who can't take (or won't get) the joke.<br /><br />This is followed by the slow and thoughtful All I Have Left Is You, which I didn't like so much initially, (I thought the slow drum beat felt a little generic at first) but it's quickly grown on me. It's not a song that many will find to be a highlight but as a fan of the occasional slow track, such as Fix You, I think it's a good addition, especially to get to hear Dexter branch out vocally in ways that I've never heard him do before. It does pick up speed as it goes and it builds to something very cool.<br /><br />OC Guns is another tongue-in-cheek track that's going to have its lovers and haters. I hated it at first but it too has grown on me. Containing everything from mariachi sounds to turntables, horns, and a whole lot of other craziness, it's definitely a mixed bag but at the same time, it's a lot of fun to jam out to. Has a cool LA flavor to it, too.<br /><br />The final act of the album is more consistent. Dirty Magic follows, a remake of their famous Ignition track that sounds great. A big part of me wishes they'd instead chosen Forever and a Day to remake off that album, but Dirty Magic's a cool song and the more powerful chorus packs a punch. I Wanna Secret Family (With You) is just a fun song, with a cheery and up-beat vibe and a fast tempo. I like it. The CD then closes off with Dividing by Zero and Slim Pickens Does the Right Thing and Rides the Bomb to Hell, two more epic punk tracks that long-time fans will definitely love. Slim Pickens is a perfect way to close off the album.<br /><br />All in all I think Days Go By is a pretty great CD from one of my favorite bands. It has just about everything I've liked about The Offspring making a return in some capacity. This includes their usual sense of humor in addition to the punk angst, so if you're hoping for nothing but the latter, you may want to adjust your expectations accordingly. Fans who love the fast and aggressive nature of the first act should let their guards down a little bit for a somewhat slower middle act; just enjoy the band having a good time, the fast songs return toward the end. Despite the jarring genre switches,Days Go By has enough on it to satisfy most everyone and I can't wait to hear these songs live.<br /><br />I'll also add that unlike a lot of albums these days, the record label has thankfully given Days Go By a proper CD jewel case instead of a cardboard sleeve, and the always-awesome Offspring CD booklet returns with lyrics and awesome illustrations and photos. Great stuff.

B007UQ5Z1G|5.0|Linkin Park return to their roots with their most personal, strongest album to date. After 4 previous albums of experimentation, they have arrived at the sound which I believe they are truly comfortable with. Although I could be wrong because all of their albums tend to be different from one another so maybe their next one won't even sound like this. Who knows? Anyway we'll cross that road when we get to it. For now let's focus on \\"Living Things\\". Right away the title of the album lets you know that they were going with a more personal approach with this album as opposed to the political concept they went with on \\"A Thousand Suns\\" and touched on briefly with \\"Minutes to Midnight\\". The songs on this album convey a lot of human emotion and it takes the listener on a personal journey.<br /><br />The sound of the album is the most unique because Linkin Park took the best elements from all of their previous albums and blended them together to create the atmosphere for this one. I first discovered Linkin Park way back when in 2000 when I was 13, and I've been hooked ever since. As a longtime fan, (they are my favorite band after all.) I've realized that there are two types of LP fans. There are the ones that have enjoyed all of their albums and those who just like \\"Hybrid Theory\\" and \\"Meteora\\" and think that everything LP has made since then sucks. Well, I think that there are elements on this album that will appeal to all fans, whether they are old, new, narrow or open minded. They do have some heavy songs on the album but never really touch the \\"nu metal\\" sound of the first two albums and of course they have some softer songs as well. So let's go through all the tracks and review them to give you a better sense of this new album.<br /><br />1. LOST IN THE ECHO- The opening song is supposed to set the tone for the rest of the album and this one does so very nicely. This song could have easily been right at home on \\"Hybrid Theory\\" or \\"Meteora\\". It's the classic LP sound infused with electronic elements. Mike Shinoda lays the raps down on the verse while Chester Bennington handles the chorus and the screams. It's the classic back and forth between these two and this song shows why these guys have such great chemistry with one another. It's also nice to hear Brad's guitars again since they were rarely used or drowned out on \\"Suns\\"<br /><br />2. IN MY REMAINS- Track two begins with some electronics, piano, and synths before blending into a cool song reminiscent of \\"Minutes To Midnight\\" Chester handles most of the vocals on this track with Mike doing backup. You can really feel the emotion in Chester's voice as he sings the words. It's a really beautiful song.<br /><br />3. BURN IT DOWN- This was the first single released for this album, so most of you should have heard it by now. For those who haven't, the backbones of this song are the synth and electronics, while the guitars blend in nicely in the background. Again Chester handles most of the vocals while a nice quick rap from Mike fills in the bridge. The wall of sound really engulfs the listener on this song.<br /><br />4. LIES GREED MISERY- This is one of the heavier songs on the album with Mike handling the verses while Chester angrily eats the chorus. During Mike's parts, he is backed up with a nice techno-like hip hop beat but when the chorus hits the guitars and drums come in to fuse everything together.<br /><br />5- ILL BE GONE- Like \\"In My Remains\\", this song sounds like it was inspired by \\"Minutes To<br />Midnight\\". It's all Chester on this one and he lets his voice soar on this song. Not too many<br />electronics on this track. This one's all rock. It's not a heavy song but it's not at all slow<br />either. Nice tune to drive to I think.<br /><br />6. CASTLE OF GLASS- If I had to pick a favorite song off of this record, it would be this one<br />frankly because it sounds like nothing LP has done before. Honestly, if Simon and Garfunkel did an LP song, it would sound likethis. That's the only way I can describe it. This song takes you on a journey. It's got an acoustic, almost folk-like sound to it backed up by suttle electric guitars. Really cool song, IMO.<br /><br />7. VICTIMIZED- An awesome song but the only downside to it is the fact that it's only 1:47 minutes long! The beginning of it sounds like something off of \\"A Thousand Suns\\" with Mike singing but then the chorus jumps in with heavy guitars and a heavy Chester chorus. Mike handles a quick little rap in the next verse followed by the chorus again and then the song ends. Just when it sucks you in, it lets you go too fast.<br /><br />8. ROADS UNTRAVELED- A nice ballad, not too slow though, and is mainly instrumental with Mike and Chester only singing a couple versus. The piano is the main instrument but as it gets going, the guitars, bass, and drums come in to create a soothing, mellow song.<br /><br />9. SKIN TO BONE- This song is backed up by a nice electronic hip hop beat but Mike isn't rapping on this one, he's singing. His singing voice has really gotten quite good. Chester joins him on backup vocals and the track is a pretty cool sounding song. The sound of the song itself reminds me of \\"A Thousand Suns\\"<br /><br />10.UNTIL IT BREAKS- Hip hop commands this track with Mike handling the rapping duties. He utilizes the Rasta style raps that he did on \\"Suns\\" and this song almost sounds like it could be a sequel of sorts to \\"Wretches and Kings\\". Chester isn't aggressive on the first chorus though as it is more soothing than heavy. Brad Delson sings the second chorus.<br /><br />11. TINFOIL- LP brings a classic element back by adding the \\"interlude\\" instrumental track that sets up the final song on the album like they did on \\"Hybrid Theory\\" and \\"Meteora\\". This sounds like a cross between \\"Session\\" and \\"Wake\\" and is just a nice little electronic-like song that seamlessly blends into the last track and lets the listener know that they are coming close to end of the album.<br/><br />12. POWERLESS- The final song on the album is a nice little ballad. You can sense the hurt in Chester's voice as he sings about someone he loved that was self-destructing and hurting him, but he felt powerless to stop it. Although it is a sad song it has a beautiful haunting sound to it. It's a nice way to end the album. Those of you who have seen Abraham Lincoln: Vampire Hunter heard a portion of this song in the end credits of the film.<br /><br />So there you have it. The rest is up to you to decide if you want this album. I say, if you are a true fan, you will love it. Linkin Park has finally arrived at a sound that they are comfortable with and the lyrics are the most powerful, personal words that they have ever written. They have come a long way since the young men that they were when \\"Hybrid Theory\\" came out, but they have matured into one of the best bands on this planet. To me, they are like a fine wine, always getting better with age. They have proved that they are a force to be reckoned with and I think that this album is their personal best. 10/10

B003Y5H5BA|4.0|In high school, Schmidt and Jenko were polar opposites: the nerd and the jock, natural rivals.  Fast forward a few years, and they become fast friends while going through police academy.  The only problem is, they're lousy cops.  But they're young looking, which makes them perfect candidates for the departmental revival of an 80's undercover program, headquartered at 21 Jump Street.  Their job: infiltrate a local high school, disguised as students, and stop a drug smuggling operation.  However, they both find that high school is not what it used to be.  Hijinks ensue.<br /><br />Surprisingly, 21 JUMP STREET is funny.  In spots, it's absolutely hilarious.  It slowly comes apart in its third act (one particular gag goes a little too far, though it's funny at first), but the first two-thirds are genuinely amusing and occasionally thoughtful.  As Schmidt, Jonah Hill tones down his usual schtick (and his body mass); as Jenko, Channing Tatum is actually hilarious (who knew he could act?!).  The actors' chemistry is undeniable (they're real-life buddies), and helps carry the film.  The supporting cast is equally strong: Dave Franco, Brie Larson, Robb Riggle, and Ice Cube stand out.  And a pair of hilarious cameos helps cap things off.<br /><br />As good as the acting talent is, the real star here is the script.  There's obviously a lot of imrpov, but the script manages to flip high school cliches on their head.  Part of the fun of the film is watching Schmidt and Jenko react to this new high school world; throw in a few high-octane scenes perfectly parodying action films, and you come up with a film that may not be brilliant, but it's at least pretty smart.  If you like hard-R comedies that have some brains behind them, 21 JUMP STREET is right up your dark alley.

B007VTVGAQ|5.0|There is only ONE Fiona Apple, period.  While there are a host of indie-pop/rock singer/songwriters, Fiona is in a league of her own.  Mysterious, artsy, and completely diverse,  2012's [[ASIN:B007VTVGAQ The Idler Wheel Is Wiser Than the Driver of the Screw and Whipping Cords Will Serve You More Than Ropes Will Ever Do]] presents Apple as creative and independent-minded as ever.  Where 2005's Grammy-nominated [[ASIN:B000B0WOEO Extraordinary Machine]] featured more orchestrations, particularly the title track, The Idler Wheel is more stripped crafting a `less is more' approach.  Despite this, The Idler Wheel is as consistent as its predecessor, even if it yields no commercial single.  That said, aside from \\"Criminal,\\" does one even categorize the enigmatic artist as commercial? Apple continues to showcase her critically-acclaimed artistry on this exceptional album.<br /><br />\\"Every Single Night\\" sets the tone of the effort, with minimal production comprised of celeste, acoustic piano, string bass, and percussion.  Apple's voice is as sultry, commanding, and vulnerable as ever, delivering every nuance with perfection.  The songwriting is top-notch and while \\"Every Single Night\\" is not `commercial' (it is a single), there is enough memorability and artistry within the lyrics to `latch onto' it and plays this cut repeatedly.  Apple doesn't compromise or miss a beat on the equally fine \\"Daredevil,\\" which opens with driving percussion.  Apple's diction is so precise, which adds to the refined nature and dramatic nature of the music.  The instrumental ideas capture here are solid and clever.  Most notably is the malicious treatment of the refrain: \\"...Don't let me ruin me/I may need a chaperone.\\"  Apple goes two for two early on.<br /><br />\\"Valentine\\" slackens the tempo, but doesn't slack up on momentum.  The cut opens with subtle thudding kick drum and piano chords giving way to bluesy-balladry.  Apple's vocals are sensitive to convey the mood.  On the refrain, ever unpredictable, Apple speeds the tempo up in which she sings: \\"I'm a tulip in a cup/I stand no chance of growing up/I've made my peace I'm dead, I'm done/I watched you live to have my fun...\\" On the superb \\"Jonathan,\\" Apple and company open up with an extended instrumental introduction.  The harmonic progression is classically-driven and is livened by interactive drums via tom tom runs.  Apple vocally sounds smoky, mysterious, and continues to deliver precise, excellent diction.<br /><br />\\"Left Alone\\" opens with pummeling tom drums, establishing a gargantuan rhythmic presence from the onset.  An excellent, though oddball piano ostinato characterizes here; overall, a jazzy sound describes the cut.  Creative and different from anything else in the music industry, \\"Left Alone\\" serves as another piece of the excellent Idler Wheel.  \\"Werewolf\\" has a six-feel about it, opening with rhythmic, lilting piano.  Apple's vocals are strong and full-bodied, affirming her genuineness as a singer/songwriter.  The refrain stands out as Apple sings: \\"But you were such a super guy til the second you got a whiff of me/we are like a wishing well and a bolt of electricity...nothing wrong when a song ends in a minor key...\\"<br /><br />\\"Periphery\\" finds Apple focuses on the lower register of the piano, a mainstay and characteristic of Apple's writing/approach.  \\"Periphery\\" possesses a `tongue-in-cheek,' novelty quality about it.  On \\"Regret,\\" Apple turns manic, particularly on the refrain in which she sings: \\"I ran out of white dove feathers/to soak up the hot p--- that comes through your mouth/every time you address me...\\" Minimalist, tasteful, and well produced, \\"Regret\\" is one of my favorites.<br />\\"Anything We Want\\" continues the overt consistency of Idler Wheel while \\"Hot Knife\\" closes the effort nearly, if not as strongly as it opens.  The layered vocals on this cut are a nice touch for sure.<br /><br />There is little if nothing to quibble about [[ASIN:B007VTVGAQ The Idler Wheel Is Wiser Than the Driver of the Screw and Whipping Cords Will Serve You More Than Ropes Will Ever Do]] ; it is Fiona at her most authentic and best.  Moody, cerebral, and creative, The Idler Wheel is easily one of 2012's best efforts and continues to find Apple growing more and more creative as time goes on. 0553801503|2.0|It's a shame George Martin felt the need to pad his previously wonderful creation with needless characters, stagnant plotting, infantile interior monologue and pointless sadism. In the previous books I felt as if MOST of the violence was justified (Jaimie getting his hand amputated, Stark losing his head, Tywin taking a crossbow bolt in the yarbles), but Book 4 left me legitimately wondering about Martin's mental health. How many loving descriptions of rapes, multilations and executions and rotting bodies should one reader suffer through? A character isn't just assaulted, she has her breasts hacked off. Two people don't just fight, one has her cheeks ripped off in cannibalistic fury. One character is served his own roasted body parts and Martin delights in describing the grease from his own flesh dripping down his mustache as he gobbles them up. You need help, Georgie boy. How did Tolkien manage thousands of pages describing a violent medieval world without umpteen references to crows eating cheeks? Bleakness for the sake of bleakness. I know Martin can do better because he DOES do better within the very same book. He includes kind and loving descriptions of Aemon Targaryen's last days and Samwell's affection for the old maester. Jaime actually shows some moral development, becoming a new and improved Lannister. So one can't abandon all hope for Martin. I have to conclude there was no artistic reason to pad this series to 7 books when Book 4 (and Book 5 if some reviews are to be believed) contain so little plot development and plentiful padding designed only to enrich his publishing bottom line.

0061020710|4.0|The Color of Magic, published in 1983, is the first book in Sir Terry Pratchett's enormously popular DISCWORLD series. The Disworld is a flat world which rides on the back of four elephants which ride on the back of a giant turtle named Great A'Tuin. The DISCWORLD novels are humorous, satirical and spoofy, often making fun of their own genre and various real-world cultural and political issues and institutions. Before HARRY POTTER, Terry Pratchett was the UK's top selling author.<br /><br />The Color of Magic introduces Rincewind who is technically a wizard because one dangerous spell attached itself to his brain when Rincewind opened a forbidden book. Rincewind doesn't know what the spell does or how to cast it, and he doesn't remember any of the other things he was supposed to learn at the Unseen University but, nonetheless, he's a wizard. He's also a coward -- a really lucky coward because, though he's unaware of it, Lady Luck is his patron.<br /><br />One day Twoflower, a rich insurance salesman from a far-off land, comes to Ankh-Morpor to vacation and asks Rincewind to show him around because Rincewind is the only person who can speak his language. Twoflower is curious, fearless, and completely ignorant of the dangers in Ankh-Morpor. Rincewind tries to safely show him the sights, but the two of them end up needing to escape from one disaster after another. During their adventures we meet a barbarian hero who loves to pose for pictures, fratricidal dragonlords with unpronounceable names (K!sdra and Lio!rt), dryads, a troll from another world, a tentacled monster who lives in a temple in which everything is octagonal but you may not say the word \\"eight,\\" a terrorist on an airplane, a drowning frog, and a group of scientifically-minded wizards who want to push somebody off the edge of the world.<br /><br />The Color of Magic is non-stop quirky adventure with lots of laughs. Pratchett's British humor is silly, clever and witty and it's fun to see him salute, and sometimes mock, well-known fantasy works, characters, or clich&eacute;s. I think I recognized Fafhrd and the Gray Mouser, Conan the Barbarian, and Red Sonja. In this first DISCWORD novel, transitions between scenes are a bit rough and sometimes the humor tries too hard, but Terry Pratchett's genius is clearly visible. The DISCWORD books are fun stand-alone reads that make a great break from heavier works.<br /><br />I listened to the 1995 audio production by ISIS Audio Books. This is not the clearest of productions -- there is a noticeable background hum (you can hear it on the sample at Amazon or Audible). However, Nigel Planer's narration was so brilliant that I will be listening to the rest of the DISCWORD audiobooks that he narrates. I loved his interpretation of all of Pratchett's characters. You should hear him pronounce K!sdra and Lio!rt.  Originally posted at Fantasy Literature.metimes mock, well-known fantasy works, characters, or clichs. It was exciting to be introduced to their world and to get a glimpse at why each was created.<br /><br />But this book isn't only about paranormals. It is about friendship, loyalty and even betrayal. The story was in no way predictable, and there were a few shocking moments which jumped out at me from nowhere.<br /><br />Although the story focuses on the MC and her issues, it was interesting to view the history of a particular minor character, through visionary flashbacks, which culminated in the explination and reasoning for what was happening to Sophia. And again, the idea of the \\"Forever Girls\\" was so imaginative and fresh.<br /><br />This story will surely satisfy its readers every desire!!

B007UQ5Z1G|4.0|Linkin Park has reached a point in their careers in which they have created a catalog of music that is so stylistically diverse and collected a fan base that is equally diverse that no matter what they release they are going to have half of their fans loving it and half of their fans hating it.<br /><br />There are two main camps of Linkin Park fans. The first group, who often refer to themselves as \\"true\\" Linkin Park fans for some unknown reason, are those nu metal fans that think Hybrid Theory and Meteora were the greatest albums ever and think that every album that the band releases should sound like those two albums and every song should make them want to put on a white wifebeater and punch people in the face. These people do not like Minutes to Midnight or A Thousand Suns... the songs on those albums are not good punching songs.<br /><br />The other camp of Linkin Park fans are real music fans who do not mind music that makes you think, rather than just rage, and enjoy having their favorite bands grow and get better through time. Don't get us wrong (I'm using \\"us\\" because I'm including myself in this group), we loved Hybrid Theory and Meteora, but we don't want the band to keep releasing the same albums over and over again. We like where the band went on Minutes to Midnight and A Thousands Suns [feel free to check out my review of A Thousand Suns]. I would actually argue that we are the \\"true\\" Linkin Park fans, as we have grown with the band and have accepted and appreciated each subsequent album instead of dismissing the band because they've changed.<br /><br />Here's the problem. The first group wants the band to release Hybrid Theory again. The second group wants the band to build off of A Thousand Suns and continue to explore new ground. There is no way for the band to release an album that is going to satisfy both of those camps. On Living Things, it sounds like Linkin Park attempted to do just that. Not surprisingly, it doesn't work.<br /><br />Living Things almost feels like two EPs on one CD. The first half of the album generally sounds like they attempted to recreate what they did on Meteora. They even threw in a couple heavy angry white boy songs like \\"Lies Greed Misery\\" and \\"Victimized\\" that will make Joe Wifebeater happy [\\"Finally, I can punch again!\\"]. \\"Lost In the Echo\\" and \\"In My Remains\\" sound like they would fit in well on Meteora. \\"Burn it Down\\" sounds as though the band was hoping for a fourth Transformers movie. \\"I'll Be Gone\\" is an excellent song, but sounds like it could've been on Minutes to Midnight. The second half of the album generally displays elements of the more recent sound the band has explored on parts of Minutes and on A Thousand Suns. \\"Castle of Glass\\" is a high point on the album and sounds very similar to their sound on A Thousand Suns. \\"Roads Untraveled\\" is great ballad-esque song, and probably my favorite song on the album. \\"Skin to Bone\\" is a very interesting sounding song, musically, and another high point on the album. \\"Until it Breaks\\" mixes a lot of styles together into multiple parts in one song, and sounds like it could've been somewhere on A Thousand Suns, it just doesn't sound as inspired as anything on A Thousand Suns did. \\"Tinfoil\\" is a transition to \\"Powerless,\\" which is another very good song with a power ballad feel (or at least Linkin Park's version of a power ballad), and a good ending to the album.<br /><br />The nu metal fans that were hoping for Hybrid Theory 2.0 will most likely enjoy about half of this album and quickly dismiss the rest of it.<br /><br />I think that overall, Living Things is a good album, but I'm disappointed in the band because I view this as a step backward for a band that has grown and gotten better on every album up until this point.<br /><br />The songs on this album are, for the most part, good; most of them will find their way onto my mp3 player, and when they play on random I will turn up the volume and enjoy them. The album as a whole,however, just feels like a band that is attempting to appease their fans rather than write what they want to write. The songs are short, less than inspired in some cases, and sound a lot like what they've done in the past. The good news is that no matter what kind of fan you are, you'll find something on here that you'll like. The bad news is that no matter what kind of fan you are, you'll also find something on here that you won't like.however, just feels like a band that is attempting to appease their fans rather than write what they want to write. B005LAIH54|4.0|This movie is entertaining, fun to watch, interesting and engaging.  The special effects are outstanding.  The numerous monsters and creatures really seem alive and present in the scenes.  There are fabulous scenes of  temples, moving mazes, and lots and lots of creatures.  The black Pegasus is back, better than ever.  (there is one marvelous scene, where an annoyed Pegasus smacks Perseus with his wing)  There is action and excitement and heroics.  The movie does not suffer from the darkness that \\"Clash of the Titans\\" had, which made many scenes hard to make out.  What it does have in common with the first movie, is the choice of colors. Really,  if you are going to film in color, how about you use, well,  some COLORS!  The entire movie is filmed in sepia tints, with only the blue sky and sea to break up the browns, rusts, sands, beiges, and blacks.  Still for all of that, the movie is well worth watching and buying.<br /><br />Spoiler Alert----Just so you know, I am going to mention specifics of the movie, what I liked and didn't, and what I thought, so if you don't like to read that kind of thing, stop here.<br /><br />The movie begins in the twilight of the gods of Olympus.  Apparently following several years after the first film, \\"Clash of the Titans\\",  the human race has continued to lose faith in the gods and to turn from worshipping them.  The gods have depended for so long on the strength given them by the faith of humans that they are all losing their powers.  The most immediate threat caused by this is that the barriers between earth and Tartarus are breaking down.  All the demons and monsters imprisoned there are escaping to rampage in the human world.  And if Kronos, the monstrous father of the elder gods, (Zeus, Hades and Poseidon) should escape, all of creation will be destroyed.<br /><br />Zeus, Poseidon and Aries go to Hades realm to confront Kronos, only to be met with treachery and death.  Zeus is captured and Poseidon mortally wounded. The other,younger gods (Apollo, Aphrodite, etc.) are all conspicuous by their absence.  This is one of the places were I wished the movie had been longer and with more detail.  Hades delivers a one line explanation that, like him, the other gods will live if they support Kronos.  This really doesn't hang together.  All the younger gods, and numerous demi-gods, all decided to run and hide, and trust their fates to Kronos?  Doesn't really track.  And if they did, wouldn't Zeus and Poseidon have noticed something wrong?  Are the younger gods already dead, or so weak that they cannot offer any support?  Nothing about them is really mentioned.  In fact, why did Zeus travel to Tartarus with so little backup?  Sure, Poseidon and Zeus are the most powerful of the gods, and maybe this is a case of hubris on their part.  And a fatal error, as they do not suspect treachery of Hades and Aries, and underestimate how much their powers have been weakened.<br /><br />The gods seem terribly human here.  I found the scenes between Zeus and Hades very touching.  There is guilt and forgiveness on both sides.  Hades' greatest fear is very telling: humans have immortal souls, that pass on after the death of their mortal bodies---but what about the gods?  Do they have souls as well, that will continue, or do they simply fade into oblivion if they should die?  A truly human fear, and an interesting thought.  Humans have their many religions and faiths to turn to in times of trial---but what of the gods?  If you are a god, and your power fails you, where do you turn for succor, if you believe in nothing greater than yourself?<br /><br />And the god Aries?  His weaknesses are truly human.  How sad it is that Aries, powerful, immortal god of war, is jealous of his half brother, Perseus.  Perseus, who has no godly power, who is not immortal, who lives in a hut and works as a poor fisherman, lucky if he has enough to eat day to day?  You would think that Perseus would be beneath Aries' notice, but Ariesis jealous because he thinks that Zeus loves Perseus more than Aries himself.  And he has allowed his bitterness to fester into unreasoning hatred. He is so fixated on hurting both Zeus and Perseus that he does not care about anything else.  And so he makes a devil's bargain with Kronos.  Supposedly Kronos has promised Hades and Aries their immortal lives, if they free him.  Both ally themselves with Kronos out of their weaknesses: Hades out of his fear of perishing forever,  Aries out of his hatred and jealousy.  And neither one of them are using their heads----when Kronos is free, why should he keep his bargains with anyone? Zeus tries to warn the pair, to no avail.<br /><br />Poseidon lives long enough to give warning to Perseus,  setting off the action for the rest of the story.  Interestingly enough, he sends Perseus to find his own half human son.  The two demi-gods ally themselves and set off to rescue Zeus and stop Kronos.<br />There are some great scenes between them, although I would have liked to see more.  The passing of the gods is very well done---they crumble to ash, leaving nothing behind.<br /><br />Liam Neeson does a wonderful job as the god Zeus, making the character regal, godly, but loving and human as well.  I am very pleased that Mr. Neeson has finally been getting the appreciation from the public that he deserves.  He appears in more movies, in better roles and with far better acting than half the so called \\"super-stars\\" of today combined.  Neeson makes the character of Zeus seem alive, both noble and human, with faults and strengths. In Greek and  Roman mythology, none of the gods were particularly noble or admirable characters, much less people who's passing you would mourn. But Liam Neeson gives Zeus all those qualities.  He has some short but truly fine scenes with Hades,  where both of the brothers ask for, and grant, forgiveness to each other.  Hades seems far less the monster than he was in the last movie. Hades realizes that he has been controlled by his fear, and has a \\"What have I done?!\\" moment.  Faced with their final ends, both gods forgive their offences against each other, and remember their loving bonds as brothers.  I loved the scenes where both godly brothers go to war against Kronos to save the world and the human race, even though they both know the probable consequence for that action. Between them, and Perseus, Kronos is destroyed and earth is saved.<br /><br />Zeus is killed, living only long enough to give a loving farewell to Perseus.  I really objected to this part of the story, although it is very dramatic.  I really thought that Hades should have been killed,  and Zeus should have survived to rebuild Olympus.  Although perhaps this was really a better punishment for Hades, as his godly powers are now mostly gone, and he may have only a short time to live.  He must face his worst fear, all alone.<br /><br />I, for one, do not believe that the gods had no souls.  No beings capable of such depths of feeling, of such great deeds, of such great hopes, could be bereft of immortal souls.  So rest in peace Zeus. And Poseidon, and yes, Hades as well.  You all did well.<br /><br />And they left the race of man behind them. Just as flawed, but just as capable of  greatness.  And perhaps we are better for it, because our accomplishments take so much more effort.<br /><br />In a way, the ending of this movie reminded me slightly of the end of the story \\"The Lord of the Rings\\".  The end of both stories see the beginning of the reign of man, and the end of all things of magic.  With the gods gone,  we have to assume that all the wonders (like Pegasus) and terrors (monsters, demons) will slowly fade away, leaving man in sole possession of the world. The torch is passed, from Zeus to Perseus, to his son, Helios.  The gods have gone, but left the half-gods, like Perseus, behind.  And they are more human than not.<br /><br />This movie was fun, a good watching experience.  I would recommend it.

B0060ZJ7BC|5.0|Billy Beane has a problem.  As general manager for the cash-strapped Oakland A's, Beane is having a hard time recruiting quality players, mainly because, with the limited budget the owner has given him to work with, he can't possibly compete with the multimillion dollar contracts being proffered by A-tier teams like the Yankees and the Red Sox.  To add insult to injury, those teams keep pilfering the few decent players Beane's already got.  Into the breach steps Peter Brand, a  23-year-old numbers-cruncher straight out of Yale who's devised a complex algorithm out of players' statistics that will allow recruiters to focus in on the less obviously flashy - and thereby far less expensive - players whom the Big Boy franchises have managed to overlook.  The skeptics question the wisdom and efficacy of reducing team-building to mere mathematic formulas and science, but Brand's method winds up working so well that it forever revolutionizes the way major league baseball teams recruit their players.<br /><br />Based on the 2003 book by Michael Lewis, with screenplay by Steve Zaillion and Aaron Sorkin and direction by Bennett Miller, \\"Moneyball\\" provides a literal inside-baseball glimpse into the inside of baseball.  In many ways, \\"Moneyball\\" is a kind of grownup version of \\"The Bad News Bears\\" and every other tale of a coach who pulls together a motley crew of misfits and second-stringers and, against all odds, transforms them into a winning team. The difference is that this story has actual history behind it, recounting the 2002 season in which the A`s won a record 20 games in a row (yet still lost in the playoffs).  Plus, the movie finds its drama more in the behind-the-scenes wrangling among the highly skeptical managers, owners, coaches and staff than in the action on the field (indeed, most of the ballpark scenes appear as grainy clips from actual games).  The intelligent screenplay avoids most of the clich&eacute;s inherent in the genre - and those it doesn't avoid it somehow manages to make seem fresh and vital again.  The writing also adds depth and dimension to Beane's character by occasionally flashing back to his own somewhat underwhelming career as a player in the big leagues, showing how that disappointment helped to mold him into the man he is today.<br /><br />Despite the sterling quality of the writing and direction, \\"Moneyball\\" is clearly an actors' picture, and the filmmakers have recruited a first-rate cast to carry out the drama (I wonder if they used a similar algorithm for that). Brad Pitt has probably never been better than he is here as the Quixotic visionary who's such a bundle of nerves that he can't even bring himself to watch his own games.  A mixture of pragmatist and romantic when it comes to the game of baseball, Beane is the perfect person to serve as iconoclast for a game whose roots lie deep in the American psyche but a game that has lost its way in recent times with its huge salaries and uncompetitive money advantages among teams.  Jonah Hill is excellent as Brand, as is Philip Seymour Hoffman as Art Howe, the A's highly skeptical and understandably disgruntled manager, who initially balks at what he believes is the disastrous direction in which Beane is taking the team.  Chris Pratt (\\"Everwood,\\" \\"Parks and Recreation\\") and Kerris Dorsey (\\"Parenthood\\") also score in small but important roles.<br /><br />There's drama and suspense aplenty in this film, with literal edge-of-the-seat excitement generated by its re-creation of the nail-biting 20th game that got the A`s into the record books.  But \\"Moneyball\\" never overplays its hand, never indulges in corny melodramatics or cheap sentiment to win us over to its side.  In fact, it is its very restraint and subtlety - both in performance and execution - that draws us so deeply into the tale it's telling.ow manages to make seem fresh and vital again. 1597801585|5.0|So many reviews have already covered this novel in excellent detail, I will simply focus on my own immediate feelings in reading it because while I was reading this novel, there were stories breaking in the news about a pesticide that has been found to kill the very bees that pollinate our crops.  Is that the small first step toward the grim reality Bacigalupi has pictured for our world 200 years from now?  Will calorie companies ultimately control the destiny of our world and societies, waging war to destroy crops and sell their own foodstuffs for profit, and stealing priceless genetic material to manufacture new crops to sell?  All of this novel felt far too real, too plausible and frightening to be mere fiction.<br /><br />There are other interesting moral questions raised in this novel.  Ever since reading 'Kiln People' by David Brin, I have pondered the ethical implications inherent in a proposed ability to create 'human-style' life forms.  In The Windup Girl, the created ones are genetically engineered to have traits not necessarily associated with standard humans.  We've already seen what happens when cats and dogs are overbred to emphasize or minimize a characteristic- we get beautiful animals with hidden physical faults and nervous personalities, losing an essential quality of the original animal.  The Windup Girl herself is one of the New People, a created creature human in aspect, but with a tendency to overheat internally, which becomes an interesting analogy to what happens when her outrage, pain and anger cause her to overheat emotionally and override her rigid training.<br /><br />In this kind of desperate society, there is no one whose hands are clean, and so there is perhaps only one heroic figure in this novel who can carry forward the banner of principle and caution. But all the others are drawn so well that it is possible to understand them and their motives, if not to like them all.  This is one of those superb science fictions novels- character-driven and based in good hard science with a compelling cautionary storyline.

B003XT603Q|5.0|The first line of the Beatles' great song, Norwegian Wood, describes the general context of Murakami's slice of  human development novel: \\"I once had a girl, or should I say, she once had me.\\" The popular Japanese author systematically sets the stage for exploration of love relationships during the critical period of ages 17 to 20 in contemporary Tokyo. During this period, people feel compelled to make lasting commitments even though they are struggling with the transition from idealism to realism, from being children to becoming adults in a competitive culture. The story of four main characters who believe they have only a small window of freedom to decide on their life paths shows readers the dangers of confusing movement with action.<br /><br />Murakami focuses on the interaction of four main characters who discover that during the late adolescent years, if they avoid the hard psychological work of making the transition from childhood illusion to adult realism, there will be lifetime consequences. The narrator, Toru Watanabe, has  a phlegmatic personality reminiscent of Thomas Mann's character, Hans Castorp, in The Magic Mountain. Like Hans, Toru is a rather naive young man from a middle class family who has learned to enjoy his youthful pleasures without making undue efforts to prepare for life's inevitable adult challenges. This avoidance of direction is reinforced by his relationship with a beautiful young girl, Naoko, who has maintained an idyllic relationship with her childhood boyfriend Kizuki even though the two realize they will not be able to live like children after their adolescent years, when they turn 20. Toru happily plays the friend of both, assuming a lackadaisical attitude and enjoying his own maturing pleasures though his self-understanding is delayed. Toru's roommate, Nagasawa is the epitome of this self-indulgent uncommitted lifestyle and Toru learns the art of using casual relationships with girls to satisfy sexual if not emotional needs.<br /><br />The ages 17 to 20 allow for exploration and preparation for adult roles, including some forgiveness for errors of judgment. But, at the end of this idyllic period, major choices loom. The characters must decide on maintaining ideals of carefree childhood at all costs (like Naoko and Kizuki), confronting the realization that they have a responsibility for accepting their own ultimate solitude in life and death (like Toru), or actively avoiding any real choices in life taking the path of least resistance to the best deal (like Nagasawa).<br /><br />Toru's favorite novel is The Great Gatsby by Fitzgerald that features a man who refuses to give up his lost youthful illusions. But, Toru rereads The Magic Mountain at a time of transitional crisis that features Hans Castorp who decides to leave the dependent life on the mountain to take on the realistic and ultimately solitary role of a responsible adult on the flatlands. The readers will greatly enjoy discovering the decisions Toru makes during his transition of what Erik Erikson called the Intimacy versus Isolation psychosocial crisis. Is Toru most like Jay Gatsby or Hans Castorp?/><br />The ages 17 to 20 allow for exploration and preparation for adult roles, including some forgiveness for errors of judgment. B007U1FEJE|3.0|I'm so glad these guys could reunite and make one last good album. Yes, I said \\"album.\\" And TWGMTR has a little bit of everything for every Beach Boys fan.<br /><br />After the gorgeous lyricless first track, there are three songs that would've been bona fide singles for the band in another era. To me, \\"Isn't It Time\\" is the freshest and most well-crafted, but, alas, it's the title track which is given top billing. While well-executed, \\"That's Why...\\" is a completely across-the-plate, mid-60s-Beach-Boys-by-the-numbers, mid-tempo song certain to get 70-year-olds on the dancefloor at VFW halls.<br /><br />Fortunately, there are also some songs for the Beach Boys fans who appreciated albums like 20/20, Friends and Sunflower. It is certifiably headphone-a-liscious.<br /><br />This long-awaited long-player also features the least filler of anything they've made since Love You (and before that, Surf's Up), which is quite a compliment, considering everything these guys (especially Brian) have been through over the years. That said, there's nothing all that special about these 12 songs (save for the closer) other than the fact that they were able to reunite and make them in the first place...and frankly, for me, that's special enough.<br /><br />My final nit with what may be this amazing band's final album of new material will undoubtedly be considered trivial and perhaps even absurd by many -- the sequencing of the songs. It's as if they let the lawyers and money guys determine the track listing. As a result, TWGMTR just doesn't flow together as deftly as so many of the band's previous efforts seemed to.<br /><br />Thankfully, that was easily fixed for me: I loaded the CD into my iTunes, then channeled my inner \\"Purple Chick\\" and re-sequenced everything, leaving only four songs where they were to begin with. I am very pleased with the end result, and I encourage you to find the sequence that feels \\"most like home\\" to you.<br /><br />For me, I thought about it in 33 1/3 terms...SIDE ONE: Think About The Days, Spring Vacation, Isn't It Time, TWGMTR and The Private LIfe of Bill and Sue, Strange World. SIDE TWO: Beaches In Mind, Shelter, Daybreak Over The Ocean, From There To Back Again, Pacific Coast Highway, Summer's Gone. I would give my own thoughtfully re-sequenced version 3.75 stars.<br /><br />And while I have absolutely no desire to catch their reunion tour oldies show (too many \\"hits,\\" not enough Brother era), I very much wish to thank Brian and the band for giving the world one more really good Beach Boys record to go along with Pet Sounds, Surf's Up, Sunflower, Love You, 20/20, Friends and the newly-released original SMILE.<br /><br />The Beach Boys will always be one of the most important bands to come from the US. 0307743659|5.0|In the early stages of Stephen King's career, he wanted to put his own twist on some of the hallmarks of the horror genre, including vampires with Salem's Lot and the haunted house story, or in this case haunted hotel, with The Shining. This horrific tale of ghosts, possession, and murder ranks as one of King's all-time scariest, and spawned the Stanley Kubrick film that most regard as a classic in its own right. Most fans are aware that King was disappointed by some aspects of that film, including its failure to establish that Jack Torrance arrives at the Overlook Hotel as a good father, a dedicated family man who would never think of bringing harm to his wife or son. In many ways, Torrance reflects the pressures and frustration King himself experienced as a young husband and father, a character prone to the same occasional impatience or anger as any normal person. However, when those frailties are placed in the hands of the malevolent forces at work in the Overlook, they become warped and distorted. Jack's descent into insanity is a gradual process initiated and controlled by external influences, a point left ambiguous in Kubrick's film. The film even hints at an inherent madness in the character before ever reaching the Overlook, so the differences from King's story are significant. Kubrick also excludes King's central metaphor of the boiler, which Jack has to release the pressure from periodically to avoid a powerful explosion. It's used in the novel to represent Jack's escalating rage as his mental instability progresses and is key to the book's plot, particularly the climax. I'm not knocking the filmmaking of Kubrick, but like most King fans, I prefer the novel. If you're looking for a scare and haven't already read The Shining, imagine the possibilities of an enormous hotel filled with malicious ghosts, a small, young family snowed in and isolated from all civilization, and the writing of a young Stephen King. One of King's top five novels.

Music is a mechanism for delivering feeling, and Williams surely excelled at that. His work is open and accessible and he worked with the music, and the concerns of ordinary people. Of course, he also wrote most of his own songs, and few have written better; several have become not just country standards, but popular music standards.<br /><br />Williams recorded but 66 songs in his brief career. Of that number, most of his great standards are here. The mournful \\"Your Cheatin' Heart,\\" \\"I'm So Lonesome I Could Cry,\\"and \\"Your Cold, Cold Heart,\\" all written by him. Also, the rollicking, good time \\"Honky Tonk Blues,\\" \\"Honky Tonkin'\\",\\"Jambalaya (On the Bayou),\\"\\"Move It On Over,\\" and \\"Hey Good Lookin'--\\" Williams wrote a lot of sad songs, but he didn't write only sad songs. There's also another song he wrote that's become a country standard, \\"Ramblin' Man:\\" those country boys sure do love the road. You'll also find on this album a couple of songs written by others: like \\"Lovesick Blues,\\" and \\"Take These Chains from My Heart.\\" They were written by others but received their definitive treatment from Williams, and will always be associated with his work: in fact, most people probably think he wrote these songs, too. If you care for country music, you'll want this album.  And it's a good buy.

B007Y6OZE0|4.0|Southern California punk-rockers The Offspring are back with their ninth album, Days Go By.  At this point in the band's career, fans probably wonder how much gas is left in the tank.  The core members are now in their mid-to-late forties - not that far away from collecting Social Security checks.  Time has a way of eroding the abilities of even the best performers.  Athletes begin to slow down, actors watch their star power recede, and musicians lose the drive and energy of their glory years.<br /><br />Fortunately, fans needn't worry about a softening of the band's sound or a slackening of the rebellious attitude that is at the heart of every punk-rock outfit.  The Offspring prove they still have plenty of game.  In fact, Days Go By is in the running for the band's best album.  Yeah, it's that good.<br /><br />Any concerns about the advancing age of the founding members are quickly put to rest after hearing the bombastic opener \\"The Future Is Now\\".  The song slams into you like a Spanish fighting bull and only lets up briefly during the piano breakdown in the bridge.  Frontman Dexter Holland vents about the dangers of technology as people become increasingly isolated from one another: \\"I sink into the night/And I'm turning off the lights/ `Cause the future is here/ This is how I disappear.\\"  One only needs to walk outside and witness the number of passers-by thumbing their smart phones to appreciate Holland's point.  Hot on its heels is \\"Secrets From the Underground\\", a breathless punk-sounding tune that unleashes the pent-up frustration from the economic stagnation that has gripped the United States.  Kevin `Noodles' Wasserman rips off a searing guitar solo before the final chorus crashes in.  The ending is tightly-focused, with Holland fuming \\"Anger starts a fiiiiiiire!\\" over a medley of pounding percussion and explosive power chords.  Two tracks in and The Offspring sound as good as ever.<br /><br />A breezy guitar hook opens the first single, \\"Days Go By\\".  It's more optimistic than the previous songs, as Holland puts forward a hopeful message that even though times are tough, things can get better.  The song stays firmly in mid-tempo territory throughout its four-minute run time, and while it doesn't measure up to some of the band's previous singles, it's still an enjoyable, easy-going song.  \\"Turning Into You\\" comes in next, propelled by a winding, distorted lead guitar layered over top of a recurring drum loop.  The theme of rebelling against the pressures of conformity will be familiar to fans of punk music, but the track has solid dynamics and energy to spare.  \\"Hurting As One\\" cements itself as the album's best track.  A spine-tingling bridge reminiscent of \\"Gone Away\\" is surrounded by a volley of unadulterated punk fury.  The chorus has equal handfuls of drive and animosity, with precise, chugging riffs and Holland layering the vocals to maximum effect.<br /><br />The middle portion of the record is a mixed bag.  There is a noticeable slowdown as some of the earlier energy begins to evaporate.  First up is the uber-catchy \\"Cruising California (Bumpin' In My Trunk)\\", which is certain to be the most polarizing song on the album.  This is an unapologetically goofy song, similar to previous oddball concoctions like \\"Pretty Fly (For a White Guy)\\" and \\"Don't Pick It Up\\".  The rapping verses and party-themed lyrics just reinforce the fact that these guys don't take themselves too seriously.  The band adopts a more serious tone on the keyboard-driven \\"All I Have Left Is You\\".  At first I didn't care much for this track - the understated nature of the song makes it easy to overlook.  It takes its time building up to the soaring finale, with Holland reflecting on two lovers holding onto each other in a storm.  The song feels very different from the material around it - quiet, introspective - but it rises up with a grand chorus at just the right time to hold your attention.  It's distinctive without being boring.  Speaking of distinctive, \\"OC Guns\\" is, quite simply, bizarre.  The song is essentially a shotgun marriage between two disparate musical styles: reggae and mariachi, with some scattered Spanish lyrics thrown in for good measure.  The end product is a weird hybrid of both styles and will likely leave most listeners scratching their heads.<br /><br />After a so-so middle section, the album begins to pick up steam as it marches to a conclusion.  \\"Dirty Magic\\" is a re-worked version of the same song from the band's second album, \\"Ignition\\" (1992).  Holland claims the band recorded the original in only three hours and they wanted to go back and put a fresh coat of paint on it.  The improved production values don't diminish the dark, haunting tone that pervades the song.  The lyrics, which focus on drug abuse and self-destruction, are creepy but well-written, and the instrumentation is biting and aggressive.  \\"I Want A Secret Family (With You)\\" has a catchy opening hook, but settles for merely being adequate as the chorus never quite sticks.  The album ends on a high note with the dual tandem of \\"Dividing By Zero\\" and \\"Slim Pickens Does the Right Thing and Rides the Bomb to Hell\\".  They sound like something The Offspring would have recorded on Ignition or Smash (1994).  Both are speedy punk-rockers that get the blood pumping and provide an emphatic statement that the band is far from done.<br /><br />Ultimately, Days Go By finds the band in top form.  The SoCal boys deliver alternating blasts of edgy punk-rock and off-the-wall zaniness with their usual flair for the dramatic.  Despite their advancing seniority, they are determined not to go quietly into that good night.  The Offspring have managed to pound out another rock-solid disc that is sure to satisfy both old and new fans alike.
